    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText3312079470141714818" style="display:none">‘Anyone who murdered Colonel Protheroe,’ declared the parson, brandishing a carving knife above a joint of roast beef, ‘would be doing the world at large a favour!’ It was a careless remark for a man of the cloth. But as Miss Marple soon discovers, the whole village seems to have had a motive to kill Colonel Protheroe.</span>

              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Your library! They have regular books, audio books and kindle books available. I do almost all my reading through the library. With digital books thes<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Your library! They have regular books, audio books and kindle books available. I do almost all my reading through the library. With digital books these days, you don't even have to go to the library in person (except to get your library card/account set up). It's a fantastic resource.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_1867832474" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1867832474" />
    <a title="Brina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2933855-brina"><img alt="Brina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601675085p2/2933855.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1867832474?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brina" href="/user/show/2933855-brina">Brina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=agatha-christie">agatha-christie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1867832474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8587954436802091738">Dame Agatha Christie is the queen of mystery writers who all modern aspirants strive to emulate. I enjoy reading her cases featuring detective Hercule Poirot because he knows the outcome well before the reader. Christie's cases are multilayered and keep unraveling until a book's conclusion. Enjoying these thought provoking cases, I decided to introduce myself to her other famous sleuth, Miss Jane Marple. There is no better place to start than Murder at the Vicarage, the book that introduced Miss</span>
  <span id="freeText8587954436802091738" style="display:none">Dame Agatha Christie is the queen of mystery writers who all modern aspirants strive to emulate. I enjoy reading her cases featuring detective Hercule Poirot because he knows the outcome well before the reader. Christie's cases are multilayered and keep unraveling until a book's conclusion. Enjoying these thought provoking cases, I decided to introduce myself to her other famous sleuth, Miss Jane Marple. There is no better place to start than Murder at the Vicarage, the book that introduced Miss Marple to the world. <br /><br />Leonard Clement along with his wife Griselda run the vicarage in sleepy village St Mary Mead. A hamlet that barely classifies as a town, all people know everyone else's business, and the vicar is looked to for guidance on all matters, religious or not. The case begins as Colonel Lucius Protheroe meets with Clement to discuss a pressing matter. Yet, before Clement can join Protheroe in his study, he finds the Colonel murdered there. <br /><br />As in Christie's cases featuring Poirot, the police assigned to this case appear to be inept at best. All of the old women in St Mary Mead believe that they can solve the crime better than the inspectors can. No meddling spinster has much to offer Clement on this cases except for his neighbor, the witty Jane Marple. Miss Marple immediately declares that she has seven suspects, but she is pretty sure she knows whodunit. As in many modern cases featuring private eyes, the police do not appreciate Marple getting in their way, and beg her off the case. Yet, she has eyes and ears everywhere, and early on it is obvious that Miss Marple will solve the case while the police are slugging through basic evidence. <br /><br />Unlike the sophisticated Poirot, Miss Marple appears as anyone's neighbor. She is a sweet older woman yet feisty and would be interesting to get to know. Whereas Poirot exercises his little gray cells, Miss Marple snoops around, her main objective to provide safety to the village that she lives in. A forerunner to today's cozy mysteries, Miss Marple appears to provide an easy reading contrast to Poirot's cases which have me thinking throughout. <br /><br />A voracious mystery reader, I did enjoy Miss Marple as a change because she could be any citizen who desires to solve a mystery. As expected she does reach the case's conclusion before the police, who are at a collective wit's end. Dame Christie is still the standard bearer for all modern mystery writers, and while I prefer Hercule Poirot, I have a feeling I will be revisiting Miss Marple as well. 3.75 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8587954436802091738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1721686609" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1721686609" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7365405-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522094190p2/7365405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1721686609?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/7365405-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6473195-the-murder-at-the-vicarage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=3-multi-book-series">3-multi-book-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=2-fic-cozy-mystery">2-fic-cozy-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=9-read-2018-04-april">9-read-2018-04-april</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=1-fiction">1-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1721686609" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5182991760292973168">A solid 4.5 stars for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16331.Murder_at_the_Vicarage__Miss_Marple__1_' title='Murder at the Vicarage (Miss Marple #1) by Agatha Christie' rel='nofollow noopener'>Murder at the Vicarage</a>, the first novel in the Miss Marple cozy mystery series, written by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie' title='Agatha Christie' rel='nofollow noopener'>Agatha Christie</a> in 1930. I've read ~ten novels by Christie and this one is near the top of the list for me. From the characters to the setting and the plot to the tone, it's an intriguing and immersive read. It started out a bit slow for me as the scene was being set, but once the murder happened, it took off in quick force. I can happily say that I had 2 potential guesses as the culp</span>
  <span id="freeText5182991760292973168" style="display:none">A solid 4.5 stars for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16331.Murder_at_the_Vicarage__Miss_Marple__1_" title="Murder at the Vicarage (Miss Marple #1) by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Murder at the Vicarage</a>, the first novel in the Miss Marple cozy mystery series, written by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Agatha Christie</a> in 1930. I've read ~ten novels by Christie and this one is near the top of the list for me. From the characters to the setting and the plot to the tone, it's an intriguing and immersive read. It started out a bit slow for me as the scene was being set, but once the murder happened, it took off in quick force. I can happily say that I had 2 potential guesses as the culprit(s), and I was correct (which doesn't always happen). I also knew there was way too much reference to 'time on clocks' for it not to be important; someone messed with the spinning needles to change the appearance of when the murder happened. But only by minutes... and you'll never guess how important it was!<br /><br />For many, this will be too on-the-nose or over-simplified when it comes to the layout at approach of Miss Marple's investigation. Though she's responsible for solving it, she's not the main character. The vicar tells us the story of what happened to the deceased, and he interacts with the detectives investigating the crime. Another priest is nearly murdered, but he's not very well liked, so it's okay, right? Some think so... but not all the 'little old biddies' (how the book refers to them) are in agreement. The gossip is out of control in this book, but I adored it for what it was -- a clever plot technique to reveal clues and keep us guessing. Add in the very peculiar marriages between the different priests and their wives, and it's baffling what life was like a century ago. But I'd give nearly anything to be part of it.<br /><br />What appeals to me most in these Marple novels is how she drops a few thoughts, then scatters around. She leaves mysterious notes for someone to come see her, then won't reveal everything she's thinking. She teases us. But it's as much fun as it is frustrating. She knows, but she's not 100% certain how... so she won't say it all at once until she's got every nasty little detail ferreted out.<br /><br />The poor vicar suffers in this one as the murder happens in his house -- everyone is up in his business. We know it can't be him or his wife, but wow do they look suspicious. Add in the side-stories and you've got one easy read. It just makes me smile to absorb these quaint settings and stories. I think even though this is the last in my April Agatha Christie Readathon, I am going to keep reading one a month this year.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5182991760292973168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_59134770" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/59134770" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/59134770?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780062234230" href="/book/show/15820438-the-murder-at-the-vicarage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=agatha-christie">agatha-christie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=audio">audio</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer59134770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15772774510846321521"><b>Miss Marple's 1st book!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1574527543ra/28498509.gif' width='400' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>But beyond <i>that</i>, this is really just a fabulous example of Agatha Christie at her best.<br/>This was my first time reading (actually <i>listening</i>) <b>The Murder at the Vicarage</b> and I was blown away by how enjoyable it was. Especially considering I've read a ton of her books and pretty much knew what to expect out of her mysteries.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1574527873ra/28498523.gif' width='300' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I knew I didn't know who <b>did</b> it, but I <i>swear</i> I thought I knew who <b>didn't</b> do it!<br/>I was (as always) dead wrong.<br/><br/>So the gist is that the town Vicar gets caught u</span>
  <span id="freeText15772774510846321521" style="display:none"><b>Miss Marple's 1st book!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1574527543ra/28498509.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But beyond <i>that</i>, this is really just a fabulous example of Agatha Christie at her best.<br>This was my first time reading (actually <i>listening</i>) <b>The Murder at the Vicarage</b> and I was blown away by how enjoyable it was. <span id="freeTextContainer10398714370521768929"><b>The Murder At The Vicarage </b>(Miss Marple #1), Agatha Christie<br/><br/>Original Publication Year 1930<br/><br/><b>Abstract:</b> Debut of Miss Jane Marple, village busybody who applies human nature to crimes. Colonel Protheroe, magistrate universally despised, was shot in his study, unheard. His wife Anne admits newly arrived artist Lawrence Redding is an old flame, and both confess to murder. The local inspector and Jane sort through to the truth.<br/><br/><b>Characters:</b> Miss Jane Marple, Inspector Slack, Lawrence Redding, Len Clement,</span>
  <span id="freeText10398714370521768929" style="display:none"><b>The Murder At The Vicarage </b>(Miss Marple #1), Agatha Christie<br /><br />Original Publication Year 1930<br /><br /><b>Abstract:</b> Debut of Miss Jane Marple, village busybody who applies human nature to crimes. Colonel Protheroe, magistrate universally despised, was shot in his study, unheard. His wife Anne admits newly arrived artist Lawrence Redding is an old flame, and both confess to murder. The local inspector and Jane sort through to the truth.<br /><br /><b>Characters:</b> Miss Jane Marple, Inspector Slack, Lawrence Redding, Len Clement, Griselda Clement, Colonel Protheroe, Anne Protheroe, Lettice Protheroe, Dr. Haydock, Mrs. LeStrange, Dr. Stone, Gladys Cram, Dennis Clement, Mary, a maid, Hawes.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و پنجم ماه نوامبر سال 1993 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: قتل در خانه کشیش، نویسنده: آگاتا کریستی؛ مترجم: فرزانه طاهری، تهران، طرح نو، 1372؛ چاپ دوم، ‏‫1387،‬‬ ‏در ‏‫372ص.،‬ ‏شابک ‏‫‭9789644890895‬؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان انگلیسی - سده 20م<br /><br />عنوان سه: قتل در خانه کشیش، نویسنده: آگاتا کریستی؛ مترجم مجتبی عبدالله‌ نژاد، نشر تهران، کتاب هرمس، کتابهای کارآگاه‏‫، 1388؛ در 307ص؛ شابک 9789643635756؛<br /><br />کشیش «لئونارد کلمنت»، راوی حوادث ناگواری است، که در «سنت‌ ماری مید» روی می‌دهد، و باعث مرگ یکی از اهالی روستا یعنی «کلنل پروترو» می‌شود؛ «کلنل پروترو»، در «سنت‌ ماری مید» شخص منفوری است، و حتی مرد محترمی مثل «لئونارد کلمنت» اعتراف می‌کند، که «هرکس کلنل پروترو را بکشد، به همه دنیا لطف بزرگی کرده»؛ حرف‌های درگوشی مردم آبادی، محور گفتگوی مهمانی چای، در اتاق پذیرایی خانه کشیش است؛ یکی از مهمانان هم «دوشیزه مارپل» است، ...؛ «قتل در خانه کشیش»، نخستین ماجراهای «دوشیزه مارپل»، و نخستین تصویری است که از روستای محبوب «سنت‌ ماری مید» ارائه می‌شود؛ «کریستی» در زندگینامه‌ اش نوشته «قتل در خانه کشیش، در سال 1930میلادی انتشار یافت؛ ولی یادم نمی‌آید کی، کجا یا چطور آن را نوشتم، یا اصلا چرا دست به نگارش آن زدم، یا چه عاملی باعث خلق شخصیت داستانی جدیدی مثل «دوشیزه مارپل» شد، و چرا چنین کسی را به عنوان کارآگاه انتخاب کردم»؛ «کریستی» گفته، دنبال خلق رقیبی برای «پوآرو» نبوده، و در ابتدا قصد نداشته داستانهای دیگری با حضور «دوشیزه مارپل» بنویسد<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 22/04/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

  <b>“The young people think the old people are fools -- but the old people know the young people are fools.”</b>

  <span id="freeText6449356576531509500" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“The young people think the old people are fools -- but the old people know the young people are fools.”</b>
</i><br /><br />THIS! <br /><br />In the tale that started it all, Miss Marple doesn’t need to move away from her lovely sanctuary in St Mary Mead. Colonel Lucius Protheroe is a loathsome creature. No one likes him, no one wants to even look at him. Therefore, the suspects are plenty once he is found murdered in the study of the local Vicar. A young artist, a flighty daughter, a troubled priest, an isolated wife, a rather posh newcomer, an archaeologist, strange clocks, portraits and paints.<br /><br />My favourite novel out of all Miss Marple’s adventures, and as always, a glorious TV adaptation (ITV 2004) where you can see the crème de la crème of British Theatre.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“What they need is a little immorality in their lives. Then they wouldn't be so busy looking for it in other people's.”</b>

<div id="review_287195403" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/287195403" />
    <a title="Jason Koivu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu"><img alt="Jason Koivu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560521450p2/1742824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/287195403?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Koivu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Koivu" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu">Jason Koivu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer287195403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5522438705640544188">Murder most proper. <br/><br/>Agatha Christie's <i>Murder at the Vicarage</i> was my first Miss Marple. Now that I've had her I can say with the experience of knowledge, she ain't half bad! Still, I'm not sure I'd want to be caught by my more macho, football playing friends reading a tea cozy mystery. The characters are dapper dandies and old teetotaler biddies. The high manners and speech abound, aside from that of the occasional parlor maid, flatfoot, or old age pensioner. Beyond primal embarrassment, this sor</span>
  <span id="freeText5522438705640544188" style="display:none">Murder most proper. <br /><br />Agatha Christie's <i>Murder at the Vicarage</i> was my first Miss Marple. Now that I've had her I can say with the experience of knowledge, she ain't half bad! Still, I'm not sure I'd want to be caught by my more macho, football playing friends reading a tea cozy mystery. The characters are dapper dandies and old teetotaler biddies. The high manners and speech abound, aside from that of the occasional parlor maid, flatfoot, or old age pensioner. Beyond primal embarrassment, this sort of thing is just a little too quaint, even for me...and I've read all of James Herriot.<br /><br />I always say I'm not into the mystery genre, but whenever I read one I'm riveted. <i>Murder at the Vicarage</i> has some clever misdirection. The murder is plausible, the details creditable and the solving of it all rewardingly confounding. I found the writing style reminiscent of PG Wodehouse. A quick bit of research showed that they were contemporaries, living through and writing within the same era. I tally this as a positive as I am a big Wodehouse fan. His work is light-handed, making for airy reading. The same can be said of the few Christies I've read. Mostly stress-free, highly enjoyable stuff that won't tax one's emotions too deeply.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5522438705640544188" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="PorshaJo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5464046-porshajo"><img alt="PorshaJo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451425289p2/5464046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1757391196?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PorshaJo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PorshaJo" href="/user/show/5464046-porshajo">PorshaJo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5464046-porshajo?shelf=challengereads">challengereads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5464046-porshajo?shelf=challengereads-2019">challengereads-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5464046-porshajo?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5464046-porshajo?shelf=agatha-christie">agatha-christie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1757391196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4480971682040728316">Fiddledesticks! How could you not enjoy a book where the word fiddledesticks is used. I'm a fan of Agatha Christie. I read her a lot when I was much, much younger. But I don't remember most of the books I read. So every now and then I plan to pick up one of her books and indulge. And what a better place to start that the first in the Miss Marple series.<br/><br/>Murder at the Vicarage tells the story of well, a murder in the vicarage. St Mary Mead is a sleep town where not much happens. However, the ladie</span>
  <span id="freeText4480971682040728316" style="display:none">Fiddledesticks! How could you not enjoy a book where the word fiddledesticks is used. I'm a fan of Agatha Christie. I read her a lot when I was much, much younger. But I don't remember most of the books I read. So every now and then I plan to pick up one of her books and indulge. And what a better place to start that the first in the Miss Marple series.<br /><br />Murder at the Vicarage tells the story of well, a murder in the vicarage. St Mary Mead is a sleep town where not much happens. However, the ladies of the town know everyone's business and it's routinely gossiped about. Leonard Clement is the vicar and his wife Griselda, well, let's just say she's not much of the lady of the vicarage house. She doesn't cook, doesn't clean, drives her husband mad, but she loves Len and he truly loves her despite the big age gap of the two. Anyway, Len returns to vicarage one night after being called away to find none other than Colonel Protheroe, dead. Murdered. I doubt many of the townsfolk are upset by this news as Colonel Protheroe was not well liked and was quite mean. But seems there are quite a number of people who might have wanted him dead. So murder...enter some bumbling police who provide great entertainment but no chance of solving this crime. But luckily, there is Miss Marple, with her keen eye, well, that comes along with being a nosy busy body. Miss Marple is quite sharp and along with the vicar, she works to solve this crime.<br /><br />What a wonderful story. I grabbed the audio and the narrator, Richard E. Grant, did an awesome job. I loved his narration and can still hear the voice of the vicar in my head. I liked the characters of Len Clement and his wife Griselda. I'm happy these two appear again in later Miss Marple books. But I had to knock it just a bit (hence 4 stars). It was so predictable, I guessed early on what happened. Though, it did not take away my enjoyment of this read. Also, there were a lot of characters to keep track of. And if I'm going to be totally honest....I prefer Poirot over Marple. But an entertaining read and great audio narration. I look forward to my next Christie book and more narrations by Mr. Grant. A quick, fun read for any Agatha Christie fan.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4480971682040728316" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3487526439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1974204871980611636">I am amazed I have not read this before. Or maybe I have but it was so long ago I have forgotten. Anyway it was really good, as good if not better than any of the other Miss Marple stories I have read.<br/><br/>It was certainly an interesting look at Jane Marple as she appeared for the first time and really as a lesser character. The main character and story teller was the Vicar, an apparently honest and caring man if a little too serious and unemotional at times. None of which prevented him being in the </span>
  <span id="freeText1974204871980611636" style="display:none">I am amazed I have not read this before. Or maybe I have but it was so long ago I have forgotten. Anyway it was really good, as good if not better than any of the other Miss Marple stories I have read.<br /><br />It was certainly an interesting look at Jane Marple as she appeared for the first time and really as a lesser character. The main character and story teller was the Vicar, an apparently honest and caring man if a little too serious and unemotional at times. None of which prevented him being in the running as a suspect. Christie managed to make me suspect almost everyone except the eventual culprits.<br /><br />No one was fooling Miss Marple though, but she kept her suspicions very close to her chest and did not declare them until every fact had fallen into place. She was a pleasure to watch as she let people assume she was a foolish old woman while actually pegging everyone's characters and behaviours very accurately. Very little gets past her!<br /><br />I love the rural English setting of these novels and the fact that they are so well written. A very pleasant way to spend a few reading hours.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1974204871980611636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3438368435" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3438368435" />
    <a title="Tim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7202176-tim"><img alt="Tim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324164999p2/7202176.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3438368435?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim" href="/user/show/7202176-tim">Tim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6473195-the-murder-at-the-vicarage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7202176-tim?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7202176-tim?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7202176-tim?shelf=1930s">1930s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7202176-tim?shelf=mystery-crime">mystery-crime</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3438368435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7139705303967906273">So, I finished this one and I've come to a conclusion... I'm not a Miss Marple fan. Yes, yes, I know, I'm one of those basic Christie fans that she couldn't stand that delights every time Poirot says something witty/arrogant, and looks at all her other characters with a "that's very nice... could you write more Poirot now?" stance. Sure, I would have been polite enough not to say that... but the thought would have occurred (that said my favorite Christie novel is <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9875107.Crooked_House' title='Crooked House by Agatha Christie' rel='nofollow noopener'>Crooked House</a> which does not fea</span>
  <span id="freeText7139705303967906273" style="display:none">So, I finished this one and I've come to a conclusion... I'm not a Miss Marple fan. Yes, yes, I know, I'm one of those basic Christie fans that she couldn't stand that delights every time Poirot says something witty/arrogant, and looks at all her other characters with a "that's very nice... could you write more Poirot now?" stance. Sure, I would have been polite enough not to say that... but the thought would have occurred (that said my favorite Christie novel is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9875107.Crooked_House" title="Crooked House by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Crooked House</a> which does not feature any of her recurring characters).<br /><br />No, let me get this out of the way, the book wasn't bad. It was entertaining enough and while I was pretty sure I knew who did it (I was right), I couldn't figure out how it was done. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[While we're on this topic, the clues were there, it felt like I must have missed a vital one somewhere because I sat there feeling like it wasn't exactly a "fair play" mystery upon the reveal. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> That said, I just couldn't really get into it. It took me over a week to read (and Christie's books usually take me about two to three days) and the only character aspect I really enjoyed was the vicar and his wife's interactions. <br /><br />This was just one of those books that I finished because I kind of felt like I had to and in the end it wasn't a bad read, it's not really one I can endorse... which is a bit sad. It's also the same way about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16298.A_Murder_Is_Announced__Miss_Marple___5_" title="A Murder Is Announced (Miss Marple, #5) by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">A Murder Is Announced</a> (the only other Marple book I've read, though I did not review it). <br /><br />There was one really good thing about this book though. It may have had the absolute best quote I've read in one of Christie's novels. While I like her as an author, I don't particularly find her quotable, but this is certainly an exception: <br /><br />“I was thinking,” I said, “that when my time comes, I should be sorry if the only plea I had to offer was that of justice. Because it might mean that only justice would be meted out to me...”<br /><br />Very nice.<br /><br />3/5 stars. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7139705303967906273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1816140812" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1816140812" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5837456-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372225128p2/5837456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1816140812?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/5837456-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1816140812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2835720239051956935">This first Miss Marple mystery is deceptively gentle, with much of the story narrated by the mild mannered vicar. When he returns to the vicarage to find the body of Colonel Protheroe shot in his study, the vicar becomes involved in the murder investigation, aided by his neighbour Miss Marple. There is a wonderful list of suspects, motives and false trails along the way, until Jane Marple untangles the threads and makes everything clear.<br/><br/>Not only is this a masterfully plotted story, but it introd</span>
  <span id="freeText2835720239051956935" style="display:none">This first Miss Marple mystery is deceptively gentle, with much of the story narrated by the mild mannered vicar. When he returns to the vicarage to find the body of Colonel Protheroe shot in his study, the vicar becomes involved in the murder investigation, aided by his neighbour Miss Marple. There is a wonderful list of suspects, motives and false trails along the way, until Jane Marple untangles the threads and makes everything clear.<br /><br />Not only is this a masterfully plotted story, but it introduces us to St Mary Mead and a cast of characters who will become familiar friends in later books. There are surly housemaids, ne'er do well poachers, gossipy old ladies and crotchety old men in abundance. As Miss Marple is keen to point out, you can see all of life quite well in a small village and nobody understands the undercurrents of life quite like she does. Wonderful fun, well written and utterly delightful, if you have never tried this series, this first book is a great place to start.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2835720239051956935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16816760673229284722">I pondered (and pondered!) my rating but have decided to go enjoyment and how good this was for the first in a series - The Divine Christie had me completely fooled!<br/><br/>There are faults - too many characters (some very similar) and the characterisation of Miss M is very uneven - she is a right old bat at the start, but by the halfway point she is the amateur sleuth I love.   <span id="freeText16816760673229284722" style="display:none">I pondered (and pondered!) my rating but have decided to go enjoyment and how good this was for the first in a series - The Divine Christie had me completely fooled!<br><br>There are faults - too many characters (some very similar) and the characterisation of Miss M is very uneven - she is a right old bat at the start, but by the halfway point she is the amateur sleuth I love. The trademark fluffiness hides great powers of observation and deduction.<br><br>Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16328.The_Murder_of_Roger_Ackroyd__Hercule_Poirot___4_" title="The Murder of Roger Ackroyd (Hercule Poirot, #4) by Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a> there is a lot more humour in this novel than most of her later ones. And an awareness of social issues. Ms Christie puts these words in one of her character's mouths;<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“We think with horror now of the days when we burnt witches. I believe the day will come when we will shudder to think that we ever hanged criminals.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br>Read with the <i>Reading the Detectives</i> group and most highly recommended!</span>

<div id="review_1470481455" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1470481455" />
    <a title="Fabian {Councillor}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40792319-fabian-councillor"><img alt="Fabian {Councillor}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599133151p2/40792319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1470481455?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fabian {Councillor}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fabian {Councillor}" href="/user/show/40792319-fabian-councillor">Fabian {Councillor}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=detective-fiction">detective-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=year-1930">year-1930</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=agatha-christie">agatha-christie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1470481455" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18371442370599518326">Who doesn't know the famous Miss Marple and her investigation talents? When it comes to well-known detectives in classic literature, along with Sherlock Holmes and Hercule Poirot she will belong to those who are mentioned first. I can almost imagine the gossipy, annoying and very inquisitive lady snooping around the village, and it's easy to understand why a smart character like her earned such a recognition beneath crime and mystery novels. "Murder at the Vicarage" is called the first book in t</span>
  <span id="freeText18371442370599518326" style="display:none">Who doesn't know the famous Miss Marple and her investigation talents? When it comes to well-known detectives in classic literature, along with Sherlock Holmes and Hercule Poirot she will belong to those who are mentioned first. I can almost imagine the gossipy, annoying and very inquisitive lady snooping around the village, and it's easy to understand why a smart character like her earned such a recognition beneath crime and mystery novels. "Murder at the Vicarage" is called the first book in the Miss Marple series, yet she only appears in a handful of scenes, irregularly interspersed in the course of this novel.<br /><br />In the first place, Agatha Christie writes about a colonel's death and the small town's vicar who tries to discover the murderer's identity. Most of the characters will at some point of the novel be suspected of being the wanted murderer, but the reader should expect the final reveal to be somehow unpredictable. I thought I had figured out who the killer was halfway through the novel, but the outcome was ... I could not have been more wrong. And it would indeed be surprising if anyone else was as smart as Miss Marple in the quest of figuring out the identity of the culprit. However, this also caused another one of this book's weak spots: Although it is only 270 pages long, it dragged on for the second half, as nearly no new information were added and the investigators were more or less left groping in the dark.<br /><br />Agatha Christie writes about very different characters trying to live in a small town where nothing ever happens - until this highly disliked man is murdered at the vicarage. As the novel is written from the first-person-perspective of the vicar, Leonard Clement, the reader has to rely on his observations, which made it even harder to guess the outcome of the murder mystery. After all, the author managed to write complicated and confusing murder mysteries with nearly no loose ends, however, something else fell by the wayside: the characters. With nearly no character development or interesting relationships present, it is hardly possible to get invested into the plot itself, and with Miss Marple being only a side character, the most interesting part of the novel was ignored for most of the time.<br /><br />My first Miss Marple novel, my second Agatha Christie novel, and still no fan of her works. I guess I'll be staying faithful to Sherlock Holmes!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18371442370599518326" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2017216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10977493059756633425"><br/>The first Miss Marple mystery. The usual red herrings and mechanical Christie plot. This early Miss Marple is more acerbic and less endearing.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1077290782" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1077290782" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1077290782?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ms. Smartarse" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse">Ms. Smartarse</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=quotable">quotable</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1077290782" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8459493880234490814">All appearances point to St. Mary Mead being the usual English small town. It has its share of colorful inhabitants, but for the most part it's a rather peaceful place. <br/><br/>There's the vicar, who, as the local sounding board, can indulge his newly discovered amateur sleuthing hobby. He is frequently accosted by several of the <em>old cats</em>, as the local busybodies are lovingly dubbed by the younger generation. And of course, we cannot forget Colonel Protheroe: most respected magistrate, as well as most d</span>
  <span id="freeText8459493880234490814" style="display:none">All appearances point to St. Mary Mead being the usual English small town. It has its share of colorful inhabitants, but for the most part it's a rather peaceful place. <br><br>There's the vicar, who, as the local sounding board, can indulge his newly discovered amateur sleuthing hobby. He is frequently accosted by several of the <em>old cats</em>, as the local busybodies are lovingly dubbed by the younger generation. And of course, we cannot forget Colonel Protheroe: most respected magistrate, as well as most despised person in town. <br><br>It is in fact the latter's murder, that rouses the town from its peaceful slumber, setting loose a sudden and unexpected chain of events.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451911849i/17620126._SX540_.jpg" alt="Fictional map of St Mary Mead" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even though I was a big fan of Dame <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/123715.Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie" rel="nofollow noopener">Agatha Christie</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/51138-hercule-poirot" title="Agatha Christie's Hercule Poirot series" rel="nofollow noopener">Hercule Poirot series</a> in high school, I have somehow never got around to reading any of her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/51798-miss-marple" title="Agatha Christie's Miss Marple series" rel="nofollow noopener">books featuring Miss Marple</a>. So what better time to tackle them, than a lengthy Christmas break? I mean, who doesn't like a dash of crime with their afternoon tea?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451911849i/17620127._SX540_.jpg" alt="Afternoon tea and scones" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Unlike the Hercule Poirot series, where the famous detective is generally sought out to help investigate the murder, Miss Marple is hardly ever requested for a consult. As a matter of fact, she is generally lumped together with the 'old cats', although the vicar <em>does</em> admit that she at least has a sense of humor.<br><br>I loved getting reacquainted with the author's typical mysteries, where I never guess the perpetrator, although I enjoy pondering the problem. I was also pleasantly surprised to discover an excellent sense of humor to go with her numerous memorable one liners.<br><br><blockquote>
<br>There is no detective in England equal to a spinster lady of uncertain age with plenty of time on her hands.<br><br>“Was bad language used?” asked Colonel Melchett.<br>“It depends on what you call bad language.”<br>“Could you understand it?” I asked.<br>“Of course I could understand it.”<br>“Then it couldn’t have been bad language,” I said.<br>Mrs. Price Ridley looked at me suspiciously.<br>“A refined lady,” I explained, “is naturally unacquainted with bad language.” <br><br>“What are you doing this afternoon, Griselda?” <br>“My duty,” said Griselda. “My duty as the Vicaress. Tea and scandal at four thirty.”<br>
</blockquote><br><br><strong>Score: 3.4/5</strong><br><br>Objectively speaking, there was nothing special in the story, but it was incredibly entertaining. I can't wait to read the following books in the series.<br><br>==============================================<br>Review of book 2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1474343555" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thirteen Problems</a><br>Review of book 3: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1482080104" rel="nofollow noopener">The Body in the Library</a><br>Review of book 4: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1492600591" rel="nofollow noopener">The Moving Finger</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8459493880234490814" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erth" href="/user/show/35848810-erth">Erth</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3191401243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17687980246085131786">Murder at the Vicarage is the first Miss Marple book to be written and published. Within the sleepy small village of St Mary Mead murder arrives when Colonel Protheroe, a much disliked prominent member of society is found dead in the study of Vicar, Reverend Clement’s study. Told through a first person narrative of Rev Clement, we observe and bumble along with the vicar the progress of the investigation to discovery of the murderer(s) through the deductions of Miss Marple.<br/><br/>A slow but delightful s</span>
  <span id="freeText17687980246085131786" style="display:none">Murder at the Vicarage is the first Miss Marple book to be written and published. Within the sleepy small village of St Mary Mead murder arrives when Colonel Protheroe, a much disliked prominent member of society is found dead in the study of Vicar, Reverend Clement’s study. Told through a first person narrative of Rev Clement, we observe and bumble along with the vicar the progress of the investigation to discovery of the murderer(s) through the deductions of Miss Marple.<br /><br />A slow but delightful story in which we view how Miss Marple’s superior powers of deductive reasoning is initially overlooked by the police, but not the reader as the vicar often draws our attention to his knowledge of Miss Marple’s sleuthing abilities. This affords the reader some superiority over the police as we have some insider information to not judge a person (old woman) by their appearance.<br /><br />Within the story I particular enjoyed the way today’s readers able to draw parallels between our society and human behaviour and that witnessed and described by Miss Marple in Post War Britain. I also enjoyed the subtle comedy which winds throughout the story in Rev Clement’s storytelling. Overall reading this book had a been lovely way to spend to couple of days.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17687980246085131786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_840896693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/840896693" />
    <a title="Carmen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen"><img alt="Carmen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412617445p2/25353295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/840896693?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen">Carmen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=traditionally-published">traditionally-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=she-says">she-says</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer840896693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10826662352446988728">Agatha Christie could have called this book a comedy as easily as she called it a mystery. She is so funny! This book had me chuckling from beginning to end.<br/><br/>Our protagonist, the Vicar, is married to a woman half his age and is always a little suspicious that she may be looking at other men. He's the long-suffering clergyman of the town - all the little old ladies come to him with their troubles and gossip - including the incredibly sharp Jane Marple.<br/><br/>Nothing even happens in the sleepy little town</span>
  <span id="freeText10826662352446988728" style="display:none">Agatha Christie could have called this book a comedy as easily as she called it a mystery. She is so funny! This book had me chuckling from beginning to end.<br /><br />Our protagonist, the Vicar, is married to a woman half his age and is always a little suspicious that she may be looking at other men. He's the long-suffering clergyman of the town - all the little old ladies come to him with their troubles and gossip - including the incredibly sharp Jane Marple.<br /><br />Nothing even happens in the sleepy little town of St. Mary Mead, so when Colonel Protheroe (an annoying and widely disliked man) is murdered by gunshot to the head, the whole town is in an uproar. It seems that no one is free from suspicion.<br /><br />Affairs, thievery, clandestine meetings, jilted lovers...good thing snoopy Miss Marple is there to keep an eye on everyone and steer the misguided police and Vicar to the correct verdict.<br /><br />Christie has a good way of bringing characters to life, filling them with quirks and speech patterns that make them spring off the page. From nosy Miss Marple, to the well-intentioned Vicar, the all-business-let's-get-this-over-with Inspector Slack, the pretending-to-be-an-idiot-beautiful-but-soulless Lettice, Christie paints a vivid portrait of country life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10826662352446988728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2525488633" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2525488633" />
    <a title="Piyangie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48056505-piyangie"><img alt="Piyangie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590579939p2/48056505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2525488633?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Piyangie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Piyangie" href="/user/show/48056505-piyangie">Piyangie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007120857" href="/book/show/282872.The_Murder_at_the_Vicarage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48056505-piyangie?shelf=classic-mystery">classic-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2525488633" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2276968166556063798">It was difficult to rate this book. I wanted to do more justice to Agatha Christie and her brilliant mind, but my conscious nags at me; it tells me that in honesty I was not drawn into the story as I normally do when I read her novels. So here I'm divided and trying to justice to her and me both. <br/><br/>It was a good plot although not a novel one. The setting is a small village in England where life is slow and stagnant. In such a small village, it is not surprising that everybody knows everybody's bus</span>
  <span id="freeText2276968166556063798" style="display:none">It was difficult to rate this book. I wanted to do more justice to Agatha Christie and her brilliant mind, but my conscious nags at me; it tells me that in honesty I was not drawn into the story as I normally do when I read her novels. So here I'm divided and trying to justice to her and me both. <br /><br />It was a good plot although not a novel one. The setting is a small village in England where life is slow and stagnant. In such a small village, it is not surprising that everybody knows everybody's business. Gossip mongers and story creators are all too common in such a closed community. In this setting, Agatha Christie brings in some interesting set of characters - old spinsters, widows, eccentric, spirited, and manipulative old and young men and women. As always, her characters are a vibrant lot. <br /><br />This is the first time that we are introduced to Christie's celebrated lady detective - the old Miss Jane Marple. Miss Marple who has made it her hobby to observe human nature rarely misses out on the important happenings in St. Mary Mead. She is sharp-witted and shrewd, and although she is no professional, it is no easy matter to delude her. <br /><br />Having read books of Poirot series, it was surprising for me to be introduced to a strikingly different detective (if I may use that word for Miss Marple). Whereas Poirot was introduced as an uncommonly brilliant detective, Miss Maple is more ordinary and reachable. It was quite a contrast to the professionalism you find in Poirot investigations. Here an ordinary old lady with her powers of observation and a decent deductive mind solves a murder-mystery which the local police fail to solve. What is interesting is that she doesn't do anything actively to gather evidence; it is that she acts upon the evidence that was gathered and thrown her way by others. <br /><br />At the onset, the story held my interest. I generally enjoyed the presentation of the incidents and characters in the tightly woven plotline. There is a fair amount of suspense from the point of murder that takes place at the Vicarage. There were incident characters and events which of course means to lead the reader in various directions when he considers who the culprit is. All was good until I got to the end. With many a twist and turns the truth is nothing but ordinary and one, I felt all along, if not for the deliberate confusion created by the author. <br /><br />It was odd how suddenly Miss Marple shines. When all the avenues of finding the murderer are exhausted, she comes forward and sums up methodically how the crime was planned and committed as if she had been in confidence with the criminals and being party to the crime. I found this brilliant summing up a little too good to be true and unrealistic. To begin with, the story is told by the Vicar. For most of the part, he plays the armature detective alongside the police inspectors. They gather evidence and all are passed to Miss Marple through the Vicar. Even medical evidence fails but Miss Marple saves the day. I'm sorry but that line taken by Agatha Christie in this story didn't agree with me. <br /><br />Nevertheless, I cannot say I didn't enjoy the story. That is something you cannot say when it comes to an Agatha Christie murder-mystery. But to speak the truth, this work didn't rise up to my expectation. I wasn't entirely drawn in. I think I was at the beginning but slowly and especially toward the end, I lost my enthusiasm. The ending was a slap in my face and I still can feel the pain it caused. It is sad, but I expected more from Agatha Christie, and I was somewhat disappointed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2276968166556063798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2099917753" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2099917753" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2099917753?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007120857" href="/book/show/282872.The_Murder_at_the_Vicarage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=mystery-and-crime">mystery-and-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=1900">1900</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-italian">in-italian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2099917753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15737201221862241501"><b>“My dear young man, you underestimate the detective instinct of village life. In St. Mary Mead every one knows your most intimate affairs. There is no detective in England equal to a spinster lady of uncertain age with plenty of time on her hands.”</b><br/><br/>It's no mystery that I am no aficionado of Miss Marple's, but with <i>Murder at the Vicarage</i>, her very first adventure, <b>I found myself gradually warming toward her</b> in a way I didn't expect. This happened, I believe, because in this novel Miss Marple is no</span>
  <span id="freeText15737201221862241501" style="display:none"><b>“My dear young man, you underestimate the detective instinct of village life. In St. Mary Mead every one knows your most intimate affairs. There is no detective in England equal to a spinster lady of uncertain age with plenty of time on her hands.”</b><br /><br />It's no mystery that I am no aficionado of Miss Marple's, but with <i>Murder at the Vicarage</i>, her very first adventure, <b>I found myself gradually warming toward her</b> in a way I didn't expect. This happened, I believe, because in this novel Miss Marple is no different from the multitude of gossip old ladies inhabiting the peaceful country village of St Mar Mead, except that she is, uncannily, way more brilliant than sharp than any of them. <b>She is a busybody through and through</b>, the kind of woman who constantly keeps an eye on the window to see who comes and who goes, the neighbour everyone would hate and dream of killing. <b>She is a complete and utter pain in the neck–unless you need her to solve some homicide</b>.<br /><br />What else can I say? Just another regular, plain day in regular, plain St. Mary Mead.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15737201221862241501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1536126837" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1536126837" />
    <a title="Duane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24389390-duane"><img alt="Duane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403316391p2/24389390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1536126837?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Duane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Duane" href="/user/show/24389390-duane">Duane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24389390-duane?shelf=2016-book-challenge">2016-book-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24389390-duane?shelf=reviewed-books">reviewed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24389390-duane?shelf=rated-books">rated-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24389390-duane?shelf=english-calssics">english-calssics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24389390-duane?shelf=mystery-crime">mystery-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24389390-duane?shelf=guardian-1000">guardian-1000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1536126837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6540110568987032262">This was Christie's 10th novel overall but the first to introduce the character of Miss Marple. She was a secondary character to the Vicar, and rightly so because the murder occurred in his study, but she ultimately does solve the mystery of "who done it". An entertaining and fun read but not considered one of her better novels.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2049275175" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2049275175" />
    <a title="Rachel Hall" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28372189-rachel-hall"><img alt="Rachel Hall" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495961295p2/28372189.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2049275175?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Hall" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Hall" href="/user/show/28372189-rachel-hall">Rachel Hall</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2049275175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6773257958662866829">It is thanks to my Goodreads friend, Roman Clodia, that I am belatedly coming to read Agatha Christie and what an utter joy she is! The debut appearance of Miss Marple in 1930 is a plotting masterpiece and full of wit and tongue-in-cheek observations which prove a delight for readers. More interesting still is the proliferation of suspects and with all and sundry in the sleepy village of St Mary Mead having expressed their antipathy to the deceased churchwarden, Colonel Lucius Protheroe, often v</span>
  <span id="freeText6773257958662866829" style="display:none">It is thanks to my Goodreads friend, Roman Clodia, that I am belatedly coming to read Agatha Christie and what an utter joy she is! The debut appearance of Miss Marple in 1930 is a plotting masterpiece and full of wit and tongue-in-cheek observations which prove a delight for readers. More interesting still is the proliferation of suspects and with all and sundry in the sleepy village of St Mary Mead having expressed their antipathy to the deceased churchwarden, Colonel Lucius Protheroe, often very vocally, suspicion looms large…<br /><br />Opening with the vicar recounting his frustrations at the “pompous old brute” - in the words of his sixteen-year-old nephew Dennis, and Protheroe’s insistence that there be an investigation into a suspected defalcation from church funds he makes a remark most unbecoming for a man of the cloth. The vicar mentions that he is expecting the “trying” Protheroe the very next evening to go through the accounts. An off the cuff riposte about the man's demise sets the tone for the sentiments of many within the village of St Mary Mead. Distractingly pretty, not in the least bit meek and incapable of taking anything seriously, the vicar’s twenty years younger wife, Griselda, then does her duty and hosts afternoon tea for the elderly spinsters of the village. Scurrilous gossip, supposition and a few choice remarks from Miss Jane Marple manages to convey the notable events and arguments that are consuming the villagers occupations. This airing of dirty linen serves as a brief introduction to the local citizens and the multitude of potential motives. And with everyone in St Mary Mead seemingly having their own differences with the Colonel and ulterior motives for implicating another party, the red herrings are plentiful as Christie shines the light of suspicion on each and everyone, making the majority of the villagers ‘fair game’ suspects. <br /><br />Narrated by the mild-mannered vicar, Len Clement, the amateur investigations which go on amongst the villagers are full of dry wit and loaded with suggestive incidents, and his unassuming manner allows Agatha Christie to make mischief and entertain her readers with some scathing remarks, all made in the disguise of being the very converse. As the village goes into amateur sleuthing mode, with no definitive record of whether shots were heard, a surly housekeeper who is loathe to be drawn into the matter and a deliberately fast clock, confusion reigns supreme. Specifying the exact dynamics of how each individual has come a cropper at the hands of Colonel Protheroe would do a disservice to what is an absolute pleasure to observe first-hand and it is Miss Marple who soon after the discovery says she can think of at least seven potential viable candidates. Unwilling to share her unproven suspicions, the all seeing and unobtrusive Miss Marple’s deductive powers prove a match for anyone, and all under the guise of her many smoke screens as a demure spinster. Early candidates range from the seemingly intentionally dreamy, Lettice Protheroe, daughter of the Colonel, through to second wife Anne and the young portrait artist charming the ladies of the village, Lawrence Redding. With Colonel Protheroe having a reputation for being firm on the bench in his capacity as local magistrate and taking a rather overbearing interest in the work of the archaeologist engaged on his land, it proves extraordinary difficult to discount the many suspects.<br /><br />A singularly deficient in humour but very zealous Inspector Slack is determined to get to the bottom of things and all under the watchful eye of the Chief Constable of the County, Colonel Melchett. Whether it is gardening, birdwatching or simply passing the time of day, Miss Marple misses nothing and her unflappable manner and habit of letting the conversation unfold naturally frequently proving revealing. As the vicar muses to himself, “for all her fragile appearance, Miss Marple is capable of holding her own with any policeman or Chief Constable in existence”. Indeed, as the vicar informs Inspector Slack:<blockquote>“My dear young man, you underestimate the detective instinct of village life. In St Mary 	Mead everyone knows your intimate affairs. There is no detective in England equal to a spinster lady of uncertain age with plenty of time on her hands.”</blockquote><br />Miss Marple herself has a rather simpler theory on her eagle-eyed skills:<blockquote>“I’m afraid that observing human nature for as long as I have done, one gets not to expect very much from it. I dare say the idle tittle-tattle is very wrong and unkind, but it is so often true, isn’t it?”</blockquote><br />As careless comments and deliberate attempts at implicating others unravel, just as I thought I was getting the measure of events and forming my own theories, Agatha Christie blindsided me with some cracking diversional tactics. Even more satisfying was that Christie took the time to address all of the puzzles which made for headaches along the way and hence tied up all loose ends and the solution is undoubtedly highly plausible. Not only does Miss Marple beat the Inspector to the solution, this first mystery sees her devising a little trap to ascertain proof of guilt and force the murderer into the open. Bravo! Outrageously good entertainment and my journey into the work of Christie is only just beginning..<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6773257958662866829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
